Die Afrika kommandowurm,
Spodoptera exempta
(Lepidoptera: Noctuidae)

Die Afrika kommandowurm is wyd
verspreid in Afrika suid van die Sahara
en is ‘n ermstige plaag in lande noord
van Suid-Afrika.
kommandowurm is die onverwagse
plaaguitbrake wat voorkom en_ lei
tot die naam “mystery worm". Groot
areas van weiding, grasperke en gras

Kenmerkend van

gewasse (by. mielies en sorghum) word
selde aangeval deur groot kolonies
van larwes. Klein vitbrake kom gereeld
voor veral in ho&reénval areas van
Mpumalanga en KwaZulu-Natal maar
groot uitbrake soos vanjaar kom slegs
elke 6-10 jaar voor. Die ergste uitbrake
in Suid-Afrika kom voor in seisoene
waar laat somer reén geval het na
droogtetoestande.

MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

The African Armyworm, Spo-
doptera exempta (Lepidoptera:
Noctuidae)

The African Armyworm is widely distri-
buted in Africa south of the Sahara,
and is a serious pest in countries north
of South Africa. A characteristic feature
of armyworm outbreaks is their unex-
pected sudden appearance, and this
has led to the common name of “mys-
tery worm”. Often, large areas of lawn,
pasture or grass crops (like maize and
sorghum) are seen to be covered in
dense colonies of larvae, virtually over
night. Small outbreaks occur frequently
in the high-ainfall areas of Mpuma-
langa and KwaZulu-Natal, but a large
outbreak such as the one this year oc-
curs only once in every 6-10 years. The
worst outbreaks in South Africa occur in
seasons where there are “late summer
rains” after drought conditions.

Moths have brown forewings and
whitish hind wings with recognized dark
brown patterns on the forewings. Moths
are capable of migrating thousands of
kilometers especially during outbreak
years. The main migration flights of the
moths start in early night time, and moths

168

ascend to a height of anything between
300-1000m above ground
Moths move downwind on prevailing

level.

air currents. In most parts of South Africa
the infestations are usually due to moths
migrating from warmer, more northerly
areas, often from Zambia, Zimbabwe
or Mozambique to South Africa. The
eggs are laid in groups of 100-400. A
single female lays several egg masses
and up to 1000 eggs. The eggs
hatch within 3-6 days depending on
temperature and humidity. Larvae can
grow to about 25mm long, are blackish
with green/yellow lines running along
the length of the body and have a cha-
racteristic V-shape mark on the front of
the head capsule. Fully grown larvae
pupate in the soil.

For effective control measures larvae
need to be detected early. If larvae are
discovered when fully grown, the use
of insecticide control is often not recom-
mended as most of the damage to crops
will already have been done, and the
likelihood that a second generation will
emerge is very small. Where larvae
move from one field to another a fur-
row can be ploughed to create a pitfall
where larvae can trapped, ploughed
under or controlled with insecticides.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute
========== p-171 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

Mieliewortelwurm

Hierdie minder bekende plaag is
al gerapporteer in KwaZulu-Natal
(Vryheid, Bloedrivier, Greytown en
Howick) en Mpumalanga (Bethal en
Piet Retief]. Onlangs is daar ook ‘n
geval aangemeld in Noord-Wes,
Koster distrik waar tot 42% van die
mielieplante op landerye beskadig is.
Die omgewing het ‘n groot rol gespeel
want die skade het voorgekom in ‘n
nuutvoorbereide land wat voorheen
‘n grasveld was. Sodra die grasvelde
vernieting word is daar geen bron
van voedsel nie en dit het waarskynlik

daartoe gelei dat die mieliewortelwurms
die gewas aangeval het.

Die mieliewortelwurm is die larfstadium
van ‘n kewer. Die kewer rig egter
geen skade aan mielies aan nie. Die
kewer is donkergrys van kleur en die
wyfies word tot 7 mm lank en 2.3 mm
breed. Die mannetjies is gewoonlik
kleiner. Eiertjies is bleek-oranje van
kleur, langwerpig en ongeveer 0.9 mm
lank en 0.6 mm breed. Die larwes is
bottergeel van kleur en silindervormig.
Die volgroeide larwes is ongeveer 10
mm lank. Die kop en laaste agterlyf

Maize Rootworm

This less known pest has been
recorded in KwaZula-Natal (Vryheid,
Bloedrivier, Greytown and Howick)
and Mpumalanga (Bethal and Piet
Retief). Recently it is also recorded in
the North Wes provice, Koster district,
with 42% damage to maize plants. The
environment played a role because
the damage was reported in a new
prepared field which previously was a
grass field. As soon as the grass was
destroyed the only source of food was
the maize plants which lead to the
rootworm attacking the crop.

The maize rootworm is the larval
stage of a beetle. The beetle does not
cause damage. The beetle is dark-grey
and the female can become 7 mm
in length and 2.3 mm in width. The
male is usually smaller. Eggs are pale
orange, oblong and on average 0.9
mm in length and 0.6 mm in width. The
larvae are a butteryellow colour and
cylindrical in shape. The fully grown
larvae are about 10 mm long. The
head and the last abdominal segment
are dark brown, the rest of the body is

covered with pale brown spots.

The eggs are laid singly or in clusters
of up to 12, either attached to grass
roots or just below ground level. The fe-
male beetle can lay up to 30 eggs and
hatch in about 15 — 18 days. During
the winter months the eggs remain in a
dormant state and hatch during spring.

174

Atter hatching, the larvae start feeding
and burrow into the subterranean stem
of the maize seedling. The larvae moult
three times after which pupal cells are
constructed in the soil. The pupal stage
is from 7 to 19 days depending on
weather conditions. There is three to
four generation per year, and the beetle
is dense in grass fields where the maize
plants had been depleted earlier in the
season by maize rootworm.

Maize rootworm could cause serious
damage to maize seedlings and re-
duce plant density to such an extent that
it might be necessary to re-plant. Plant
density could be reduced by as much
as 80%, but infestation usually only af
fects certain patches in the field. The
pest becomes particularly serious dur
ing years when good spring rains are
followed by a long, relatively dry pe-
riod. The first visible damage symptoms
observed are similar to those of maize
infested by black maize beetles or false
wireworms. Firstly, the whorl wilts and
dries after which the entire plant wilts
and dies. Some plants survive these at
tacks by producing a lot of useless tilt
ers. Damage symptoms under the soil
include larvae burrowing a tunnel into
the mesocotyl of the maize seedlings
and feed a range of holes into the stem
below the soil surface. When more
than one larva is on a plant, some lar-
vae may leave the plant, crawl over the
soil surface and bore into neighbouring
plants.

Bagrada Besie

‘n Onbekende insekplaag op mielies
is onlangs in die Noordwes-provinsie
opgemerk. Die spesie is geidentifiseer
as die Bagrada besie (Bagrada hilaris).
Oor die algemeen is hierdie spesie ‘n
plaag op koolgewasse en geen geval
is bekend waar mielies al in die verlede
aangeval is nie. Die skade kom kolkol
in landerye voor. Die voorafgaande ge-
wasse kon moontlik ‘n rol gespeel het in
die uitbraak van hierdie plaag. Voorat
gewasse was rape, lusern en hawer
wat moontlik die bron van_infestasie
kon veroorsaak.

primére  plantgasheerspesies ~waarop
hierdie besie voed behoort aan die
Brassicaceae familie. Dit is ook al

gewasse (sekondére gewasse] aan
val wat naby ‘n brassica gewas met
besiebesmetting geplant word.

Bagrada Bug

An unknown insect pest on maize is
recently reported in the North West
province. The species is identified as
the Bagrada bug (Bagrada hilaris).
This species is usually a pest on cab-
bage crops with no reports of maize
being attacked. Damage is only re-
corded in certain patches in the field.
The previous crop planted, radish, lu-
cerne and oats, can explain the pos-
sible source of infestation.

The Bagrada bug has — sucking
mouthparts. The primary host plants
on which this bug feeds belong to the
Brassicaceae family. It is also reported
that this pest can attach other crops
(secondary crops) where brassica crops
do have high infestation levels.

Hatchlings are 1 mm in length and de-
velop quickly into adults that reach 5 —
7 mm. The bug is black with orange-red
markings over the entire body. Adults
have wings, but rarely flies and can
walk considerable distances to infest
new plants. Females lay their eggs on
the ground or less commonly, on foli-
age. The eggs are white and then turn
orange. A female bug can lay more
than 100 eggs which can hatch with
in a weeks’ time. The nymphs take two
to three weeks to reach maturity. A few
generations may be produced per sea-
son if conditions are favourable.

Bagrada bug are gregarious and feed
in groups. The adults and nymphs at

180

tack above-ground plant parts. The
bugs have sucking mouthparts with
which plant fluids are suck from green
plant material. However, they do not
inject toxins to the plant. Damage symp-
toms differ between different crops.
Feeding result in white or yellow mark-
ings where feeding have taken place.
The damage can usually been seen at
the outer edges of the leaves. The outer
edges may dry out and turn brown if
damage is severe.

The cultivation of soils where brassica
crops have been planted may help re-
duce the viability of eggs that are laid
on the soil. Old leaves or harvested
crops should be destroyed which can
be a source where nymphs survive. In
the case of conservation farming where
no or minimal soil disturbance take
place the use of a contact insecticide
being sprayed on the soil can be used
to control nymphs and adult bug.

Further reading:

Annecke, D.P. and Moran, V.C. 1982.
Insects and Mites of Cultivated Plants in
South Africa. Butterworhts, Durban/
Pretoria.

Visser, D. 2009. A Complete Guide to
Vegetable Pests in South Africa. Agri-
cultural Research Council, Roodeplaat

Vegetable and Ornamental Plant Insti-
tute, Pretoria. Po 102 — 106.

INDRINGER INSEK SPESIES / INVASIVE INSECT SPECIES

Herfs/Amerikaanse-Kommandowurm /
Fall armyworm

Eiers: Koepel vormig met plat basis, kurf op-
waarts met ‘n breér ronde punt. Eiers word gelé
in 'n eierpakkie wat geheg word op blaaropper-
vlak. Mot kan tot 1000 eiers lé. Wytie mot maak
eierpakkie toe met 'n laag grysskubbe. Eiers
broei uit na 2 — 3 dae (Fig. 29 en 30).

Larwes: Groen van kleur en verander van kleur
soos larf groei. Larwes varieer in kleur, lig bruin,
groen tot amper swart. Drie geelwit lyne is teen-
woordig oor die lengte van die rug. Kenmerkend
is ‘n Y-vorm op die voorkop (Fig. 31). Larwale
stadium kan so kort as 14 dae wees.

Papie: Word papie in die grond maar kan ook
blare aanmekaar weef. Larf bou 'n papiesel met
grond om in 'n papie te word. Papiestadium is
tussen 8 — 10 dae.

Mot: Motte is sterk vlieérs en het 'n vlerkspan
van 32 — 40 mm. Aktief in die nag. Voorvlerke
van die mannetjie mot is skakeerings van grys en
bruin met ‘n driehoekige wit merk op die punt
en naby die middel van die vlerk. Wytievlerke is
vaal en het nie opvallige merke nie. Agtervlerke
is silver-wit in beide geslagte. Volwasse stadium
is sowat 10 dae.

Skade: Larwes veroorsaak ernstige skade aan
blare as ook direkte skade aan pluim en koppe.
Kan skade aanrig aan byna alle stadiums van
die mielieplant maar konsentreer gewoonlik op
mielieplante wat nog nie baard het nie. Mees
algemene skade word aangerig voordat pluime
sigbaar is. Mielieplante herstel gewoonlik van
kelkskade. Tydens blomstadium kan larwes ge-
deeltelik of tenvolle die jong koppe vernietig. Ge-
woonlik word skade kol-kol in mielieland gevind.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

Fig.30.

Fig.31.

Fig.32.

181

========== p-184 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

Eggs: Dome shaped with a flat base, curves up-
ward to a broadly round point. Eggs are laid in
egg batches attached to foliage. Moth can lay
1000 eggs. Female moth deposits layer of greyish
scales over the egg batch. Eggs hatch within 2 - 3
days (Fig. 29 and 30).

Larva: Green with colour change as larvae ma-
ture. Larvae vary in colour from light tan, green to
nearly black. Three yellow-white lines run down the
larva back. Charactiristic with inverted Y-shaped
on the forehead (Fig. 31). Larval duration can be
as short as 14 days.

Pupa: Pupation normally take place in soil but can
also take place by webbing together leaf debris.
Larvae constructs a cocoon in soil to pupate in.
Pupal stage is about 8 — 10 days.

Moth: Strong flyers and have a wingspan of 32 —
40 mm. Active during the night. Forewings of male
moth is shades of grey and brown, with triangular
white spots at the tip and near the centre of the
wing. Female forewings are less distinctly marked.
The hind wings is silver-white in both sexes. Dura-
tion of the adult stage is about 10 days.

Damage: Larvae cause serious leaf feeding dam-
age as well as direct injury to tassel and ears. Can
cause damage to nearly all maize stages but con-
centrate on maize that have not yet silked. Most
common damage is to late pretassel maize. Maize
plants often recover from whorl damage. With tas-
selling larvae may partly or totally destroy young
ears which is more important than leave damage.
Usually damage is found in patches in the field.

VOORDELIGE INSEK SPESIES / BENEFICIAL INSECT SPECIES

Wespe/wasp
Cotesia sesamiae

Klein wespes (4-6mm) val stamboorder-
larwes aan. Nadat die wytie die stam-
boorder geparasiteer het deur eiertjies
binne in die liggaam van die larf te
l8, ontwikkel klein wespe-larfies in die
stamboorder. Daarna kom die wespe
larwes uit die stamboorder uit en vorm
kokonne waaruit die wespes dan weer
kom. Daar kan ongeveer 20 - 30
wespe larwes uit een stamboorder kom.

Small wasps attack stem borer species.
Atter the female wasp has parasitized
the stem borer larvae by laying eggs in-
side it, wasp larvae develop in the stem
borer. Wasp larvae then emerge from
the stem borer to spin cocoons. From
these cocoons wasps again emerge.
Approximately 20 - 30 wasps can
come from one stem borer.

Kokonne voordat wespes uitkom/Cocoons before wasps emerge

Parasitiese vlieg / Parasitic fly
Sturmiopsis parasitica

Hierdie parasitiese vlieg val ook ver-
skeie plae aan tydens die larf stadium.
Daar kom oor die algemeen slegs een
vlieg maaier uit ‘n larf wat aangeval is
deur ‘n vlieg maar daar is al gerapor
teer dat tot vyf maaiers uit een larf kan
kom. Sodra vliegmaaiers byvoorbeeld
uit 'n stamrusperlarf kom word hulle pa-
pies wat weer oorsprong gee aan ‘n
vlieg.

184

This parasitic fly attacks various pests
during their larval stage. Overall only
one fly maggot emerges from a pest
larva but up to five maggots have been
reported. Maggots emerge from for ex-
ample stem borer larvae and pupate to
become flies again.

Maaier besig om uit stamboorder larf te kom/Maggot emerging from
stem borer larva

Oorkruipers / Earwigs

Oorkruipers het kouende moddele en is
goeie predatore wat 'n wye reeks insek-
plae aanval. Oorkruipers gebruik hul
knypers om hul prooi te vang en begin
dan vreet aan die prooi. Wyties |é so-
wat 50 eiers in ‘n nes onder die grond
en voorsien die nimfe van kos totdat hul
groot genoeg is om die nes te verlaat.

Earwigs are good predators with chew-
ing mouth parts. They attach various
kinds of insect pests. Earwigs use their
pincers to attack prey and then start
feeding. Females lay about 50 eggs in
burrows and care for their early nymphs
by proving them with food until they are
big enough to survive on their own.

Oorkruiper wat stamboorder aanval/Earwig attacking stem borer

Tierkewers / Tiger beetles
Carabidae

Tierkewers is ook predatore wat kou-
ende monddele het waarmee hulle hul
prooi aanval. Tierkewers is ingestel op
beweging en kan prooi selfs groter as
hulself aanval. Hul prooi kan bestaan
uit sekere ander kewers, larwes, miere,
sprinkane en spinnekoppe.

Tiger beetles are also predators with
chewing mouth parts with which they
attack their prey. Their vision is acute,
as any movement causes the beetle to
turn and face the source of motion, they
can also attack prey that may be larger
than themselves. Beetles, larvae, ants,
grasshoppers and spiders are just a few
of their reported prey.

Tipiese tierkewer/Typical tiger beetle

PLANT PARASITIESE AALWURMS OP MIELIES

INLEIDING

Die meeste produsente is bewus van
die teenwoordigheid van plantpara-
sitiese aalwurms maar aalwurmsimp-
tome is nie altyd spesifiek nie en
kan maklik verwar word met tipiese
simptome wat deur plaagdoderskade,
versuiptoestande en voedingstekorte
veroorsaak word. Die impak wat
aalwurms op ‘n mielieoes kan hé,
word daarom dikwels nog onderskat.
Uit ‘n opname wat tydens die
2008/2009 regoor die
mielieproduksie gebied uitgevoer is,

seisoen

is sewentien aalwurm groepe op die
mielies geidentifiseer. Vir die doel van
hierdie handleiding sal daar egter
net op twee groepe wat die mees
algemeenste op mielies voorkom,
gefokus word.

Knopwortelaalwurms is die mees

Oorlewing

As daar nie ‘n geskikte gasheer beskik-
baar is nie, kan knopwortelaalwurms
wel op verskeie onkruide wat alge-
meen in ‘n mielieland voorkom, voort
plant en oorleef. Knopwortelaalwurms
se belangrikste oorlewingsstrategie
gedurende die winter is egter om in
onuitgebroeide eiers wat in die grond
en in plantreste wat na oes in die land
agter gelaat is voorkom, te oorleef. Die
eiers is instaat om vir ‘n onbepaalde
tyd in die rustoestand bly en sal slegs
uitbroei as die toestande weer gunstig
vir die aalwurm is.

2. Letselaalwurms
(Pratylenchus spp.)

Letselaalwurms is sporadies maar as
hulle wel voorkom, is dit gewoonlik in
hoé getalle en daarom kan hierdie aal-
wurm nie onderskat word nie. Plaaslik
kom P. zeae en P. brachyurus die mees
algemeenste voor op mielies en word
naas knopwortelaalwurm as die be-
langrikste aalwurms op mielies geag.
Van die twee letselaalwurmspesies rig

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

die meer patogeniese P brachyurus
die meeste skade aan. In gevalle waar
altwee spesies egter in dieselfde land
voorkom, sal die minder patogeniese
P. zeae 'n groter deel van die bevol-
king uitmaak omdat sy lewenssiklus
korter is, hy vinniger kan voortplant
en ‘n hoér tolleransie vir ‘n wyer reeks
temperature het. Beide spesies floreer
egter in ‘n wye reeks grondtipes. Vog
is ‘n faktor wat ‘n belangrike rol speel
in die voortplanting en skadepoten-
siaal van letselaalwurms, wat dikwels
gedurende die reénseisoen kan ver-
hoog.

Simptome wat met letselaal-

word

‘n beduidende

Bogrondse simptome is egter nie baie
spesitiek nie omdat die voorkoms
van die simptome bepaal word deur

soos die simptome by die knopwortel
aalwurm, in kolle voorkom en nooit
eweredig regoor die land versprei
wees nie.

Wortelskade deur letselaalwurms kan
dikwels geidentifiseer word deur die

wat op die worteloppervlakte voorkom.
Die epidermis waar al die wortelhare

gevorm word, word vernietig as
die aalwurm voed. Dit kan tot erge

plant water en voedingstowwe swak
opneem. Letsels kan ook deur fungi en

word.

Oorlewing

As klam  grond_ toegelaat word
om stadig uit te droog, kan beide
letselaalwurm spesies in anhidrobiose
ingaan. Anhidrobiose is ‘n rustoestand
waarmee die letselaalwurm in staat
is om vir byna ses maande deur
droogteperiodes te oorleef. Hierdie
oorlewings-strategie stel die aalwurm
in staat om die tydperk tussen twee
mieliegroeiseisoene suksesvol te kan
oorleef. Anhi-drobionte sal weer aan
die begin van die reénseisoen ten
volle herstel sodra die mielies begin
ontkiem. Die oor-grootte meerderheid
van die populasie oorleef egter die
droé seisoen in onuitgebroeide
eiers. Die eiers sal slegs uitbroei as
die mielies begin ontkiem en die
omgewingstoestande gunstig is vir die

aalwurm om te oorleef en te ontwikkel.

190

VERSPREIDING VAN
AALWURMS

Aalwurms is mikroskopies klein en
kan nie vreeslik ver op eie stoom
beweeg nie. Hulle moet dus op
ander maniere staatmaak om te kan
versprei van een land na ‘n ander
toe. Water is waarskynlik een van
die mees effektiefste metodes wat
die aalwurm gebruik om mee te kan
versprei. Vater vanaf lande wat reeds
met aalwurms be-smet is asook water
van besproeiingskanale en damme
kan lande wat deur die kanale en
damme bedien word, herbesmet.
Aalwurms kan ook op die mens reken
om hom rond te dra en te versprei.
Grond en soms ook plantreste wat aan
implemente of skoene van werkers wat
in besmette lande gewerk het vassit,
kan eiers bevat wat dan weer na 'n
volgende land toe oorgedra word.

DIE BESTUUR VAN AALWURMS
OP MIELIES

Dit is feitlik onmoontlik om die hele aal-
wurmpopulasie in ‘n land uit te roei.
Daar sal altyd ‘n klein hoeveelheid
eiers en/of wurmpies oorleef, ongeag
die beheermaatreél wat ‘n produsent
toepas om hulle te probeer beheer.
Die hoof doel van aalwurmbestuur is
eerder om die aalwurmgetalle in ‘n
land laag genoeg te hou sodat die
skade wat deur hulle veroorsaak word
nie lei tot ekonomiese verliese vir die
produsent nie (hou die aalwurmpopu-
lasie onder skade- en ekonomiese
drumpelwaardes). Die volgende be-
heermaatreéls kan gebruik word om
aalwurmpopulasies onder skade- en

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute
========== p-193 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

ekonomiese drumpelwaardes te hou.
As twee of meer van hierdie beheer-
maatreéls met mekaar gekombineer
word, sal dit net nog meer voordele vir
die produsent inhou:

Chemiese beheer

Die meeste produsente steun nog
steeds swaar op chemiese beheer om
aalwurms in bedwang te hou. Huidig-
lik is carbofuran, carbosulfan en terbu-
fos as nematisiedes op mielies geregi-
streer en kan slegs met plant toegedien
word. Dit is uiters belangrik om die
instruksies op die etiket tot op die letter
na te volg om sodoende die minimum
impak op menslike en dierlike gesond-
heid sowel as op die omgewing uit te
oefen,

Onvoorspelbare omgewingstoestande
(bv ‘n onnatuurlike hoé reénval) lei
daartoe dat die effektiwiteit van che-
miese middels vir die beheer van aal-
wurms nie altyd gewaarborg kan word
nie. Produsente word dus ten sterkste
aangeraai om die gebruik van nema-
tisiedes verkieslik met nog 'n beheer-
maatreél te kombineer.

Wisselbou

Wisselbou is een van die belangrikste
beheermaatreéls beskikbaar vir die
produsent. Nie net kan wisselbou die
aalwurmgetalle onder beheer hou nie
maar dit kan ook die mikrobiese diver-
siteit in die grond verhoog en die natuur-
like vyande wat die aalwurms weer
op hulle beurt aanval, vermeerder.
Die beplanning van ‘n effektiewe wis-
selboustelsel hang egter af van die
aalwurmspesies wat teenwoordig is

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

en om bewus te wees van die gasheer
voorkeure van daardie spesifieke aal-
wurmspesies. ‘n Suksesvolle wisselbou
sisteem sal die vatbare gewas (by mie-
lies) opvolg met swak gashere of met
gewasse wat glad nie gashere vir die
aalwurmspesies is nie.

Weerstandbiedende kultivars

Weerstandbiedende kultivars is ‘n koste
effektiewe, omgewingsvriendelike be-
heermaatreél| wat maklik in reeds
bestaande plaagbeheerprogramme in-
gesluit kan word. Dit is weereens es-
sensieé| om te weet watter aalwurm-
spesies in die land voorkom omdat
kultivars slegs weerstand teen een van
die spesies mag hé. Waar moontlik en
indien beskikbaar is dit 'n goeie keuse
om weerstandbiedende kultivars in ‘n

bestaande produksiesisteem in te sluit.

SAMEVATTING

Onvoorsiende faktore soos uitermatige
hoé reénval of die gebrek daaraan,
onvoorspelbaretemperatuurskommelinge
en grondtekstuur kan gunstige toestande
vir die aalwurm skep om in te floreer
al het die produsent al die reéls tot op
die letter nagevolg. As ‘n produsent
dus vermoed dat
beperkende faktor is wat voorkom dat
hy die maksimum oesopbrengs van
sy gewas verhaal, word dit aanbe-
veel dat daar grond en wortelmonsters
na die LNRInstituut vir Graangewasse
toe gestuur word sodat dit geanaliseer
kan word vir die teenwoordigheid van
plantparasitiese aalwurms.

PLANT-PARASITIC NEMATODES ON MAIZE

INTRODUCTION

Most producers are aware of the pre-
sence of plantparasitic nematodes
but symptoms resulting from nematode
damage are not always specific and
can easily be confused with symp-
toms typically associated with damage
caused by pesticides, water logging
and nutrient deficiencies. The impact
of nematodes on maize yields is, there-
fore, often under estimated. From a sur-
vey conducted all over the maize pro-
duction area during the 2008/2009
growing season, seventeen nematode
groups have been identified to be as-

sociated with maize. However, for the
purposes of this information guide only
the two most important genera com-
monly present in maize fields will be
discussed.

IMPORTANT PLANT-PARASITIC
GENERA ASSOCIATED WITH
MAIZE

1. Root-knot nematodes
(Meloidogyne spp.)

Rootknot nematodes are the most

prominent genera throughout the maize

Fig.1. Above-ground symptoms of maize in a nematode infested field

192

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

(Foto: Dr Chris Schmidt: Sidi Parani)
========== p-195 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

production area. A typical rootknot
nematode population in a maize field
consists of mixed M. incognita and
M. javanica populations. Both species
have a wide host range, which means
that they can parasitise and develop on
crops other than maize. Under optimal
conditions a rootknot nematode female
can hatch from its egg and be ready
to lay eggs in approximately 20 to 25
days. A single female can produce over
1 000 eggs during her lifetime. Da-
mage that is already inflicted on the
roots will, therefore, remain irreversible.
The damage and reproduction potential
of rootknot nematodes often increase
during the rainy season, especially in
seasons where an unnaturally high rain-
fall occurs.

Fig.2. Root-knot nematode females

(white) inside root tissue

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

Symptoms associated with root-
knot nematode infestation

Aboveground parts of plants infested
with rootknot nematodes are stunted,
yellow and patchy in growth. These
symptoms can typically be seen as yel-
low patches in the field that will never
be evenly distributed (Fig. 1). In severely
rootknot nematode infested fields plants
may die before harvest.

Galls formed on the roots by feeding
rootknot nematode females (Fig. 2) are
not always visible and depends on the
species as well as the number of nema-
todes feeding on the plant. Therefore,
the absence of galls is not always indi-
cative of the absence of rootknot nema-
tode populations. If the galls are indeed

(Foto: Dr Chris Schmidt: Sidi Parani)

Fig.3. Galls formed by root-knot
nematodes on maize roots

193
========== p-196 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

visible (Fig. 3), it can be identified fairly
easily on the roots and range in size
and numbers. The galls are formed from
giant cells induced from normal plant
cells through feeding of the female.

Survival

In the absence of a suitable host crop
rootknot nematodes are able to survive
and reproduce on many weed spe-
cies commonly found in maize fields.
However, the main survival strategy of
rootknot nematodes during the winter
months is to survive in unhatched eggs
present in the soil and in plant residue
left behind in the field after harvesting.
These eggs may stay in this resting
phase for an unpredictable time and
only hatch when conditions are favou-
rable.

2. Lesion nematodes
(Pratylenchus spp.)

Lesion nematodes occur sporadic but
when they do occur, it is usually in high
numbers and can therefore not be un-
derestimated. P. zeae and P. brachyurus
are the most common lesion nematode
species associated with maize and se-
cond only to rootknot nematodes. Of
these two lesion nematode species, P.
brachyurus is the most pathogenic and
causes the most damage. However,
when both species occur together in a
field, the less pathogenic P. zeae will
dominate P. brachyurus because of its
shorter life cycle, faster reproductive

194

rate and higher tolerance to a wider
range of temperatures. Both species
thrive in a wide range of soil types.
Moisture is an important factor affecting
the reproduction and damage potential
of these lesion nematodes, which can
increase during the rainy season.

Symptoms associated with le-
sion nematode infestation

Plant height and chlorophyll content in
the leaves are generally considerably
reduced. Aboveground symptoms are,
however, not highly specific because
symptom expression is affected by the
species present, the number of nema-
todes present at the time (population
density) and environmental conditions.
If aboveground symptoms do occur, it
will be in patches like that of rootknot
nematode symptoms.

Root damage by lesion nematodes can
often be diagnosed by the presence
of small lesions on the root surface.
The feeding of the nematodes on the
roots causes destruction of the epider-
mis, which is where the root hairs are
formed. This may cause severe necro-
sis and damage to root hairs, which
leads to a poor uptake of nutrients and
water by the plant. Lesions caused by
lesion nematodes can also be infected
with fungi and bacteria (secondary in-
fection). Symptoms caused by lesion
nematodes on the roots are difficult
to identify because it can be masked
by and confused with symptoms other
than that caused by nematodes.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute
========== p-197 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

Survival

When moist soil is allowed to dry out
slowly, both
cies are able to enter anhydrobiosis.
Anhydrobiosis is a resting phase in

lesion nematode  spe-

which the lesion nematodes are able
to survive almost six months of drought.
This survival strategy enables the nema-
tode to effectively survive the period
between two maize-growing seasons.
Anhydrobionts will return to full activity
at the start of the rainy season when
maize seeds start to germinate. Most of
the population however, survives the dry
seasons in unhatched eggs, which will
only hatch when the seed starts to ger
minate and environmental conditions are
favourable for the nematode to survive
and develop.

DISTRIBUTION OF THE NEMA-
TODES

Nematodes are microscopically small
and cannot move long distances on
their own. They must, therefore, rely
on factors other than their own loco-
motion to move them from one field to
another. Water is probably the most
effective agent in distributing nematodes.
Water from nematode infested fields
and even that from irrigation channels
or dams can re-infest fields serviced by
those channels or dams. Nematodes
can also rely on humans to carry them
around. Soil and sometimes also plant
rests on implements and on shoes of
workers working in infested fields can
contain eggs, which will then be trans-
ferred to the next field.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

MANAGEMENT OF NEMATODES
ON MAIZE

It is almost impossible to completely
eradicate a nematode population in
a field. A small number of eggs and
or nematodes will always survive,
irrespective of the means by which
a producer tries to control them. The
main aim of nematode management
is, therefore, to keep the numbers of
the nematodes in the field low enough
so that the damage they cause do not
translate into economical losses for the
producer (keeping the nematode popu-
lations below damage and economic
threshold levels). The following ma-
nagement tools will help the producer
to keep nematode populations below
threshold

levels. Using two or more of these tools

damage and economic
in combination with each other will
provide even more advantages to the
producer and will lessen the risk:

Chemical control

Most producers still rely heavily on che-
mical control to keep nematodes in
check. Carbofuran, carbosulfan and
terbufos are currently registered nemati-
cides for nematode control on maize
and can only be applied at planting.
Care should be taken to follow the in-
structions on the label to the letter to
ensure minimum impact on human and
animal health as well as on the environ-
ment.

195
========== p-198 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

However, with unpredictable environ-
mental conditions (eg. an unnatural
high rainfall) the efficacy of nematicides
for nematode control cannot always be
guaranteed. Producers are therefore
strongly urged to preferably combine
the use of nematicides with another
management tool.

Crop rotation

Crop rotation is one of the most impor-
tant management tools available to the
producer. Not only can crop rotation
keep the nematode numbers under con-
trol, it can also increase the microbial
diversity in the soil and increase the
numbers of natural enemies that attack
the nematodes. However, an effective
crop rotation system depends on the
nematode species present and to know
the host preferences of the nematode
specie. A successful rotation system will
then include the susceptible crop (eg.
maize) followed up by poor or non-host
crops.

196

Resistant cultivars

Resistant cultivars are a costeffective,
environmentally friendly management
tool that can easily be incorporated
into existing pest management pro-
grammes. Once again it is essential to
know the nematode species in the field
since cultivars may only be resistant to
one of the species. It will be a good
choice to incorporate a resistant cultivar
in the production system where possible
and when available.

CONCLUSIONS

Even though a producer may follow
every detail to the letter, factors such as
a high rainfall or total lack thereof, un-
predictable temperature ranges and soil
texture may provide favourable condi-
tions for nematodes to thrive. If a pro-
ducer therefore suspects that nematodes
might be a limiting factor in obtaining
the maximum yield from his crop, it is
recommended to send soil and root
samples to ARC-Grain Crops Institute to
be analysed for the presence of plant
parasitic nematodes.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute
========== p-199 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

MONSTERNEMING VIR PLANT PARASITIESE AALWURMANALISES

Omgewingsfaktore en selfs bewer-
kingspraktyke kan veroorsaak dat
aalwurmpopulasies handuit
ruk en groot skade aan gewsse aan-
rig. As ‘n produsent vermoed dat aal-

wurms die sondebok is wat veroorsaak

dikwels

dat hy ‘n verlaagde opbrengs en/of
oeskwaliteit athaal, kan hy grond- en
wortelmonsters na die LNRnstituut vir
Graangewasse toe stuur sodat dit vir
plantparasitiese aalwurms geanaliseer
kan word.

Wanneer is dit die beste tyd om
monsters vir aalwurmanalises
te trek?

Aalwurmpopulasies bereik hulle piek
in terme van aalwurmgetalle sodra
‘n eenjarige gewas begin blom.
Daarna begin die populasie stadig
maar seker af te neem as gevolg van
verskeie faktore soos byvoorbeeld ‘n
kompetiesie tussen mekaar vir kos
en minder gunstige omgewingstoe-
stande. Die beste tyd om aalwurm-
monsters te neem, is dus wanneer
die gewas begin blom. Die enigste
uitsondering is grondbone. Anders as
die ander aalwurmspesies, piek peul-
aalwurmpopulasies (die belangrikste
grondboonparasiet) eers met oes-
tyd wanneer die oorgrote meerder-
heid van die populasie in die peule
voorkom. Grondbone moet dus eers
met oes gemonster word.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

Hoe moet die monsters getrek
word?

Dit is baie belangrik dat daar grond
en wortels teenwoordig moet wees.
As daar net grondmonsters ingestuur
word, kan net die aalwurms wat op
daardie tydstip in die grond voorkom,
geidentitiseer word. Op so ‘n manier
gaan baie van die wortelparasiete wat
mees-al net in die wortels voorkom, ver-
lore. Die tellings sal dan nie ‘n betrou-
bare weerspieéling van die werklikheid
gee nie. As dit 'n gewas soos grond-
bone of groente is wat hulle oes onder
die grond dra, moet daar van die
peule/knolle ook ingesluit word. Hoe
meer monsters van ‘n land af getrek
word, hoe beter die kanse dat daar ‘n
ware weerspieéling van die aalwurm-
bevolking gekry kan word. Monsters
kan in ‘n zig-zag patron getrek word,
veral in kolle wat simptome vertoon.
Kostes kan ‘n rol speel, daarom verkies
baie produsente om van hierdie mon-
sters bymekaar te gooi, dit te meng en
dan ‘n verteenwoordigende monster(s)
te stuur.

Hoe moet die monster gehan-
teer word?

Die hele plant moet uitgespit word so-
dat die grond rondom die wortelstelsel
behoue kan bly (Fig. 1). Die aalwurms
sal in die grond direk om die wortel
stelsel voorkom omdat dit is waar hulle
kos kry. Die laboratorium het ongeveer
200 cm’ (200 ml) grond per monster

201
========== p-204 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

nodig vir ekstraksie. As die hoeveel-
heid grond rondom die wortelstelsel
baie meer as dit is, kan die oortollige
grond liggies afgeskud word (Fig. 2).
As daar nie genoeg grond rondom die
wortelstelsel is nie, skep nog bietjie
grond met die hand uit waar die plant
uitgespit was en plaas dit in 'n plastiek-
sak (Fig. 3). Bogrondse gedeeltes van
die plant moet afgeknip word omdat
dit nie nodig is vir aalwurmekstraksies
nie (Fig. 4 & 5}. Plaas nou die wortel
stelsel met die grond in ‘n plastieksak
(Fig. 6). Merk die oorsprong van die
monster op die plastieksak duidelik aan
die buitekant met ‘n merkpen, want dit
is die verwysing wat die laboratorium
sal gebruik (Fig. 7). Van hier af moet
die monster in die koelte gehou word.
As dit nie dadelik na die laboratorium
toe gestuur kan word nie, kan dit vir ‘n
dag of twee in die yskas gehou word.

Monsters kan per koerier gestuur word
na of afgelewer word by: LNR-Instituut
vir Graangewasse, Hendrik Schoeman
Gebou, Chris Hani 114, Potchefstroom,
2520. 'n Folio met die kontaknommers
en e-pos adresse of besigheidskaartjies
moet in die pakkie ingesluit word sodat
die kliént gekontak kan word. Merk die
pakkie vir aandag: Sonia Steenkamp.

Wat gebeur met die monster na-
dat dit afgelewer is?

Die grond en wortels word nou ver
werk (Fig.8) sodat die aalwurms uit die
grond en wortels geekstraeer kan word
[Fig.9). Vir elke grond en wortelmonster,
sal daar drie ekstraksies gedoen word:

202

1. Aalwurms sal met behulp van die
suiker flotasie metode vanuit die
grondmonster ge-ekstraeer word.

2. Al die

parasiete (die aalwurms wat in die

plantparasietiese endo-

wortel self voorkorn) behalwe die
knopwortelaalwurms sal uit ‘n 5g
wortelmonster ge-ekstraeer word,
ook met die suiker flotasie metode.

3. Die metode wat gebruik word om
knopwortelaalwurms vanuit 50g
wortelmonsters te ekstraeer (die aan-
gepaste NaOCl metode] is spe-
siaal aangepas omdat die knop-
wortelaalwurm wyfie sakagtig is
en kan nie soos die res van die
wurmagtige aalwurms ge-ekstraeer
word nie.

Die aalwurms wat uit die grond en
wortelmonster geekstraeer is, word dan
geidentitiseer en getel (Fig. 10).

Wat is die kostes hieraan ver-
bonde?

Die koste van elke ekstraksie sal
R250.00 (BIW ingesluit) beloop. Dus,
die groottotaal van ‘n volledige wortel
en grondmonster sal R750.00 beloop
(R250.00 x 3 ekstraksie metodes).

Wanneer sal_ die resultate

beskikbaar wees?

Die analise van die monsters sal tussen
drie en wf werksdae neem waarna die
kliént ‘n verslag van die resultate sal
ontvang.

SAMPLING FOR PLANT PARASITIC NEMATODE ANALYSIS

Environmental conditions and even

cultivation methods often cause
nematode populations to increase and
cause significant damage to crops. If
a producer suspects that nematodes
could be the reason for a decline in
yield and/or yield quality, soil and
root samples can be send to the ARC-
Grain Crops Institute for plantparasitic

nematode analyses.

When should samples be taken
for nematode analyses?

Nematode populations reach their
peaks in terms of numbers as soon as
annual crops start to flower. After that
the population will steadily decline as a
result of factors such as intra competition
for food sources and less favourable
environmental conditions. The best time
for nematode sampling will, therefore,
be at flowering of the crop. The only
exception is groundnut. Compared to
most of the other nematode species,
pod nematode populations (the most
important nematode on groundnut]
only peak at harvesting where the main
portion of the population will be present
in the pods. Groundnut must therefore
be sampled at harvesting.

How should the samples be
taken?

It is important that soil as well as roots

208

is included in the sample. If only soil
samples are analysed, only those
parasites present in the soil at that time
can be identified. Root parasites that
are present only in roots will then be lost
and the counts will not reflect a reliable
indication of the nematode population
in the field. If the crop e.g. groundnut
or vegetables carries its yield below the
soil surface, pods/tubers must also be
included. A high number of samples
ensure a more reliable reflection of the
nematode population. Samples can be
taken in a zig-zag pattern, especially
in patches with sick plants. Costs of the
analysis can play a role so producers
can mix the samples and then take a
sub-sample for analysis.

How should the sample be
treated?

The whole plant should be removed
from the soil in such a way that the soil
around the root system remains intact
(Fig. 1). The nematodes will be pre-
sent in the soil directly around the root
system because that is the zone where
they will feed. The laboratory will need
approximately 200 cm$ (200 ml) soil
per sample for nematode extractions.
Excess soil can be lightly shaken off
the root system (Fig. 2). If there is not
enough soil available around the root
system, soil can be collected from the
area in which the plant has been sam-
pled and placed in a plastic bag (Fig.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute
========== p-211 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

3). Above ground parts of the plant can
be removed since it is not needed for
nematode extraction (Figs 4 & 5}. Place
the root system together with the soil
into the plastic bag (Fig. 6). Mark the
origin of the sample in the bag on the
outside of the bag using a marker (Fig.
7). This information will be used as re-
ference by the laboratory. From this step
on forward, the sample must be kept in
the shade. If it cannot be send immedi-
ately to the laboratory, it can be stored
in the refrigerator for one or two days.

Samples can be couriered or delivered
at: ARC-Grain Crops Institute, Hendrik
Schoeman Building, Chris Hani 114,
Potchefstroom, 2520. Please include a
folio or business card with contact num-
bers and e-mail addresses so that the
client can be contacted. Mark the pack-
age for attention: Sonia Steenkamp.

What happens to the samples
after delivery?

The soil and roots will now be pro-
cessed (Fig. 8) so that the nematodes
can be extracted (Fig. 9). For each soil
and root sample, three extractions will
be conducted:

1. Nematodes will be extracted from
the soil using the sugar flotation
method.

2. All plantparasitic endoparasites
(nematodes present in the root tis
sues} except root knot nematodes
will be extracted from 5g root

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

samples using the sugar flotation
method.

3. An adapted NaOCl method will
be used fo extract root knot nema-
todes from 50g root samples. This
specially adapted method is used
to extract the rootknot nematodes
because the sack like female can-
not be extracted from the roots like
the other, vermiform nematodes.

The extracted nematodes will then be
identified and counted (Fig. 10).

How much will the extractions
cost?

Each extraction will cost R250.00
(VAT included). The total of a complete
soil and root extraction will amount
to R750.00 (R250.00 x 3 extraction
methods}.

When will the results be

available?

The analyses of the samples will take
between three and five working days
after which the client will receive a re-
port.

========== p-212 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

ALLES EN MEER OOR
HOUTSKOOLVROT

Houtskoolvrot word nie alleenlik
geassosieer met mielies nie, maar ook
met sojabone, sonneblom, sorghum,
katoen, tabak asook ongeveer 500
ander plantspesies. Meeste produsente
sou al waargeneem het dat hierdie
siekte prominent was gedurende warm,
droé seisoene, veral na blomtyd. Om
te verstaan hoekom dit gebeur, asook
hoe om hierdie kennis te benut om
die voorkoms van die siekte beter te
bestuur, moet beide die plant en die
patogeen verstaan word.

Cor die algemeen het aangetaste plante
‘n olyfgroen kleur, wat ‘n aanduiding
is dat daar probleme in die wortels
en stamme is. Wanneer sulke stamme
oopgesny word, word die kenmerkende
houtskoolverkleuring waargeneem
op die onderste nodes van die plant
(Fig. 1.). Die simptome wat geassosieer
word met houtskoolvrot is as gevolg van
die teenwoordigheid van klein swart
sklerotia, wat op die vaatbondels en
die binnerand van die stam ontwikkel

(Fig.2.). Sklerotia is die
oorlewingsstrukture van Macrophomina
phaseolina, die —_ veroorsakende

organisme van houtskoolvrot en dit stel
die swam in staat om op stoppel te
oorleef.

Die rede waarom houtskoolvrot meer
geneig is om voor te kom in droér
seisoene, is gesetel in die toestande
wat die patogeen verkies om onder te
groei en te infekteer. Macrophomina

phaseolina  floreer onder warm,

210

droé toestande, veral vanaf die
blomstadium. Die  siektegraad van
die siekte is gevolglik groter wanneer
die omgewings- en grondtemperatuur
toeneem (28-35°C) asook wanneer
grondvog beperkend raak. Wéreldwyd
wil dit voorkom of die gebied waar die
siekte voorkom besig is om toe te neem
weens klimaatsverandering.

1

n  Toename in _houtskoolvrot
gepaardgaande met droogtetoestande
tydens blomperiode word deur
kundiges — verklaar = deur _— die
‘fotosintetiese — stremmingstranslokasie
balans’ beginsel. Volgens hierdie
beginsel, word die plant meer vatbaar
vir wortel en stamvrot na blom weens
koolhidraattekorte = wat — voorkom
wanneer die plant onder stremming
verkeer. Eenvoudig gestel, die plant se
fokus is om sy koppe te vul. VWanneer
die plant weens stremming (bv. a.g.v.
vogtekorte) nie in staat is om die nodige
koolhidrate te produseer nie, begin dit
‘n proses van ‘selFkanibalisme’ deur die
gestoorde koolhidrate in die stamme na
die koppe te vervoer. Hierdie proses
veroorsaak dat die stamme verswak
en dus meer vatbaar word vir watter
patogeen cok al in die omgewing
is — wat in ons huidige scenario M.
phaseolina is, ‘n patogeen wat, soos
reeds genoem, baie goed kan infekteer
onder sulke ekstreme warm droé
toestande.

Wat nou gemaak as die siekte eers
posgevat het in jou land? Normaalweg
word wisselbou gebruik om siektes
te beheer, met die idee dat wanneer
nie-gasheergewasse geplant word, dit
die patogeen as't ware "uithonger”’

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute
========== p-213 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

deur nie vir hom iets te gee waarop
hy kan voed en voortplant nie. Soos
reeds genoem, het M. phaseolina 'n
wye gasheerreeks en is die patogeen
in staat om alle gewasse wat tans
kommersieel verbou word te infekteer
(Fig.3.). Wisselbou sal dus nie effektief
wees om die siekte te bestuur nie.

Gesiene dat alle stamvrotte
normaalweg geassosieer word met
stremmingstoestande, bly die goue
reél rakende die bestuur van die siekte
om toestande te beperk wat stremming
teweegbring. Soos met verskeie siektes,
is gasheerweerstand die beste metode
om die siekte te bestuur. Sou sulke
inligting nie beskikbaar wees nie, moet
produsente seker maak dat die kultivar
wat gekies is, goed aangepas is vir
die omgewing, omdat so ‘n_kultivar
reeds ‘n genetiese voorsprong het
wanneer dit met stremming te doen kry.
Weerstand teen blaarsiektes, goeie
stabiliteit_ en droogtetoleransie sowel
as hoé opbrengspotensiaal sal dus
help om die voorkoms van stamvrotte
beter te bestuur. Hou by die aanbevole
plantdigthede van die kultivar. Té hoé
plantdigthede en nou rywydtes sal
bydra tot stremmingstoestande wat
ideaal is vir infeksie.

Besproeiingskedules is baie belangrik,
veral vanaf blom. Navorsing het
getoon dat toeneem
wanneer watertoediening verminder
of gestaak is voor graanvulling voltooi
was. ‘n Gebalanseerde beskikbaarheid
van stikstof. ~regdeur die
kan die voorkoms van

stamvrotte

seisoen
stamvrotte
verminder, terwyl ‘n tekort aan kalium

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

(wat ‘n belangrike rol speel in die
fotosinteseproses), die voorkoms van
stamvrotte kan verhoog. Stamboorders
en blaarsiektes moet beheer word,
want dit kan bydrae tot die stremming
waaronder die plant verkeer. Baie
onkruide dien verder ook as gashere vir
hierdie patogeen en moet dus beheer
word.

Produsente moenie onverhoeds deur
die siekte betrap word nie. Lande
moet gereeld gemoniteer word vanaf
30-40% graanvog deur die integriteit
van die laer stamnodes te toets. Sou
dit voorkom of stamvrot ‘n probleem is,
moet pogings aangewend word om
so vroeg moonilik te oes, omdat plante
wat omval kan lei tot addisionele kostes
om die graan geoes te kry.

Bewaringsboerdery kan __laastens
gesien word as ‘n__ bruikbare
beheerstrategie om houtskoolvrot te
beheer. Bewaringsboerdery bestaan
uit drie beginsels wat toegepas word
en sluit in minimum grondversteuring,
die behoud van ‘n deklaag en
wisselbou. Deur die deklaag te behou,
word die risiko van siektevoorkoms
verhoog, weens die feit dat baie
siekteveroorsakende organismes,
waaronder grondgedraagde
plantpatogene, op plantreste kan
oorleef. Verminderde bewerking wat
met bewaringsboerdery geassosieer
word kan dus daartoe bydrae dat siektes
toeneem, veral waar mieliemonokultuur
toegepas word. Navorsingsbevindings
deur die LNR Graangewasse op
‘n bewaringsboerderyproef in die
Venterdorp (sanderige

211

omgewing
========== p-214 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

leemgrond, Hoéveld area, Noord-Wes
Provinsie] het egter aangedui dat die
deklaag ook voordelig kan wees in die
bekamping van sekere siektes. Hierdie
navorsing het getoon dat die deklaag
bygedra het daartoe dat plante minder
stremming ervaar het met die voorkoms
van laatseisoen droogtetoestande. Dit is
weens beter waterinfiltrasie en -retensie
wat geassosieer word met die deklaag,
wat ‘n invloed het op die vermoé van
die patogeen om te infekteer. Koriom,
dit maak die omstandighede vir infeksie
ongunstig. Wisselbou is egter ‘n vereiste
met bewaringsboerdery.

Konsensus rakende klimaatsverandering
is dat Suid-Afrika in alle waarskynlikheid
eerder warmer en droér sal word
as koeler en natter. Gepubliseerde
navorsing het reeds gerapporteer dat
Suid-Afrika ongeveer 2% warmer en
ten minste 6% droér was oor ‘n tien-
jaar periode wat gestrek het vanaf
1997-2006, in vergelyking met die
1970s. Dieselfde navorsing het getoon
dat die land as 'n geheel ‘n 1.1.%
val in mielieproduksie kan ervaar vir
elke 1% val in reénval. VWanneer in
ag geneem word dat hierdie warmer
en droér toestande ‘n impak sal hé op
biotiese faktore, word voorspel dat
seker siektes meer prominent sal word.
In hierdie verband kan houtskoolvrot 'n
reuse impak hé in die Suid-Afrikaanse
landbousektor en produsente sal dus
hul bestuurspraktyke moet aanpas om
plantstremming te verminder.

THE ‘INS’ AND ‘OUTS’
OF CHARCOAL ROT

Charcoal rot is a disease most
commonly associated with stalks of not
only maize plants, but also soybean,
sunflower, sorghum, cotton, tobacco
and approximately another five hundred
other plant species. Most producers
would have observed by now that the
disease is much more prominent during
the hot and dryer seasons, especially
when the conditions prevail from the
period after flowering.
understand why this happens, and how
to use this knowledge to manage the
disease, one must understand both the
plant and the pathogen.

In order to

In general, infected plants would have
a wilted olive green appearance,
normally the tell-tale signs of problems in
the roots and stalks. When cut open, the
stalks have the characteristic charcoal
discoloration at the lower nodes of the
plant (Fig. 1.). The symptoms associated
with charcoal rot is due to the presence
of numerous, minute, black sclerotia,
particularly on the vascular bundles
and inside the rind of the stalk. These
sclerotia give the stalk a grey/black
appearance from which the disease
gets its name (Fig.2.). Sclerotia are the
survival structures of Macrophomina
phaseolina, the causal organism of
charcoal rot, allowing it so survive on

stubble.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

As to why the disease is most common
in drier seasons, the answer lies in the
conditions favoured by the pathogen
to. grow and infect. Macrophomina
phaseolina simply flourishes under
hot, dry conditions. The severity of
the disease has been documented
to increase as ambient and soil
temperature increases (28-35°C) as
well as when soil moisture becomes
limiting. Worldwide it is reported that
the area where the disease is occurring
is increasing due to climate change.

Internationally, researchers explain as to
why the disease is most common during
the period following flowering through
the ‘photosynthetic. stresstranslocation
balance’ concept. According to this
concept, plants become more subject
to root and stalk rot after flowering
due to carbohydrate deficiencies that
occur in these plant parts under stress
conditions. Simply put, the plant is
focused during this period on filling its
ears. Should the plant not be able to do
so, due to e.g. limited water, it starts
selfcannibalising, by moving already
stored carbohydrates from its stalks to
the ears, accordingly predisposing the
stalk to infection by whatever pathogen
is in the vicinity — which in our current
scenario is M. phaseolina, a pathogen
quite happy to infect under such extreme
hot and dry conditions.

So what to do when the disease
has taken hold of your precious
crop? Normally integrated disease
management strategies include crop
rotation with non-hosts. The non-

213
========== p-216 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

host plant is supposed fo starve the
pathogen by withholding ‘food’ from
it, As, however, stated, M. phaseolina
is capable to infect all major crops
currently utilized in crop rotation systems
[Fig.3.]. Crop rotation will accordingly
not solve the problem and producers
will have to be smart about tackling this
disease. As all stalk rots are generally
linked to stress conditions, the golden
thread throughout the management
of such a difficult pathogen is to
limit the amount of stress the plant is
exposed to. As with many diseases,
host resistance would be a feasible
method to manage the disease. If such
information is not available, ensure that
the cultivar selected is well suited for
the area, as such a cultivar will have
a genetic advantage when having to
cope with stresses. Resistance against
leat diseases, good stability, drought
tolerance as well as a high yielding
potential are all qualities that will give
a cultivar a genetic advance and
could help to indirectly control stalk
rots. Stick to the recommended plant
densities as determined by the cultivar
selected, soil fertility, available soil
moisture as well as the production
potential of the area. Too high plant
densities and too narrow row widths
will create stress conditions ideal for
infection. Irrigation schedules are very
important, especially post flowering.
Research has demonstrated that stalk
rot increased when water application
was reduced or ceased before grain
filling has been completed. A balanced
availability of nitrogen — throughout
the season can reduce the level of
stalk rot experienced, whilst a lack of

214

potassium (K) (which plays an important
role in photosynthesis), can enhance
the level of stalk rot experienced. Stalk
borers and leaf diseases should also
be controlled as they will contribute to
plant stress experienced. Many weeds
also serve as host to this pathogen and
should also be controlled.

Do not get caught off guard by
this disease. Productions should be
monitored regularly, from approximately
30-40% grain moisture. The integrity of
the lower nodes should be tested and
should it be apparent that stalk rot is a
problem, attempts should be made to
harvest the plants as early as possible,
as lodging will result in additional costs
in order to get the grain harvested.

Conservation agriculture (CA) could
lastly be seen as viable management
tool for the control of charcoal rot.
Generally, CA consists of a combination
of practices that include minimal soil
disturbance (notill), permanent soil
cover (mulch) and crop rotation. A risk,
however, always present with CA is the
potential of disease development as
many soilborne pathogens survive on
plant residue. Reducecttillage practices
associated with CA accordingly create
the risk of increased disease incidence
and resultant yield loss, especially
where maize monoculture is practiced.
Recently reported research findings by
ARC-Grain Crops Institute of a CA trial
conducted on a sandy loam soil in the
Ventersdorp area (Highveld area, North
West Province), however, indicated that
all is not just doom and gloom when it
comes to CA and disease. From this

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute
========== p-217 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

research it became apparent that the
cover layer associated with CA helped
to reduce the stress experienced by
the plants during late seasonal drought
conditions that were experienced. This
was due to better water infiltration and
retention associated with the cover
layer. This finding corresponds to
international research findings which
reported significantly higher incidences
of stalk rot caused by M. phaseolina
in conventionally tilled — treatments
when compared to those in notill
treatments. The better water infiltration
and retention associated with the cover
layer associated with CA practices
could accordingly have an effect on the
capability of this fungus to infect and
are accordingly seen as a viable way
to manage the disease, provided that
crop rotation is practiced.

regarding — global
warming and the impact that it will
have on South Africa's climate, is that
South Africa will more likely become
hotter and drier than cooler and wetter.
Published research already reported that
South Africa has been approximately
2% hotter and at least 6% drier over
a ten-year period which spanned from
1997-2006, compared to the 1970s.
The same research has indicated that
for the country as a whole, each 1%
drop in rainfall would most likely lead
to. a 1.1% drop in the production of
maize. When considering the impact of
warmer and drier conditions on biotic
factors, it is foreseen that some diseases
and pests will become more prominent
as the climate becomes hotter and drier.
In this regard, Charcoal rot might very

The consensus

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

well be the next game changer in the
South African agricultural industry and
producers should accordingly adjust
their management practices to reduce
plant stress.

maize crowns and stalks

PROBLEME MET LANDBOUMIDDELS:
WAT STAAN DIE BOER TE DOEN?

Voordat die afleiding gemaak kan
word dat ‘n landbouchemiese-middel
nie aan die verwagtinge volgens
registrasie voldoen nie, moet die pro-
dusent sekere feite nagaan. Daar moet
verseker word dat aan al die inligting,
gebruiksaanwysings en waarskuwings
wat op die etiket verskyn, voldoen is.
Byvoorbeeld:

1. Stem die weerstoestande tydens en
na die toediening ooreen met die
toestande soos voorgeskryf?

2. |s die tyd van toediening nagekom,
byvoorbeeld vroeg in die oggend
of laat namiddage

3. Val die toestand en aard van die
grond waarop die gewas verbou
is binne die raamwerk van die
voorskrifte, byvoorbeeld tipe grond
en grondvoge

4. |s die beheermaatreéls teen die
onkruid toegepas op die groeista-
dium soos deur die gebruiksaan-
wysings voorgesknyfe

5. |s die aanbevole dosis van die mid-
del toegedien soos voorgeskryf?

6. Is die — landboumiddel wel
geregistreer op die — betrokke
gewas en teen die spesifieke
onkruid, swam of plaag?

PROBLEMS WITH AGROCHEMICALS:
WHAT SHOULD THE FARMER DO?

Before assuming that an agrochemical
does not comply with the expectations
of registration, the producer should first
It should be en-
sured that all directions and warnings

establish certain facts.

appearing on the label were followed.
For example:

1. Did the environmental conditions
during and after application corre-
spond with those as prescribed?

2. Was the time of application com-
plied with, i.e. early in the morning
or late afternoon?

3. Did the conditions and nature of
the soil where the crop was grown
fall within the framework of the pre-
scribed conditions, i.e. soil type
and soil moisture?

4. Were the control measures against
the problem applied to the crop
growth stage prescribed in the in-
structions?

5. Was the recommended dosage

of the chemical applied as pre-
scribed?

6. Was the agrochemical definitely
registered on the specific crop and
against the specific weed, fungus
or pest?

218

IF YOU ARE STILL CONVINCED
THAT YOU HAVE A PROBLEM,
FOLLOW THE GOLDEN RULE: DO
NOT PANIC.

1. Immediately contact the representa-
tive or agent where the chemical
was purchased.

2. Confirm your complaint in writing
to the relevant company.

3. Insist on an in loco investigation.

4. If the problem is not solved:

(a) Immediately arrange that a neutral
scientist (not a legal person) i.e.
someone from an agricultural co-
op, Agricultural Research Council,
University or the Government visit
the site together with the relevant
company to discuss the problem.
This should not be done when the
symptoms have disappeared or at
harvesting.

Notify the Registrar: Act 36. of
7947, Private Bag X343, Pretoria,
0007 of the problem. Telephone
(012) 319 7303.

(b

(c) If the company does not respond,
notify AVCASA at PO Box 1995,
Halfway House, 1685. Telephone
(012) 805 2000. Email: info@
croplife.co.za (Follow up in writ

ing).

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute
========== p-221 ==========
MIELIE-INLIGTINGSGIDS | MAIZE INFORMATION GUIDE | 2017

(d) Notify GSA (012) 807 6023 /
08600 47246 or the ARC-Grain
Crops Institute (018) 2996100 of
the problem and what steps have
been taken. (Follow up in writing)

5. If you are still not satisfied, you are
free to commence with legal ac-
tion.

(a) Investigations and findings by the
Registrar Act 36 of 1947, only de-
termine whether criminal or penal
action should be taken.

(b) AVCASA can only request their
members (chemical companies] to
react to a claim if a producer feels
that he is being ignored.

6. Remember that a civil court action
which has been taken against a
company is completely separate

from criminal actions by the Regis-
trar: Act 46 of 7947.

Information gathered by the Registrar is
for his office use only, unless ruled oth-
erwise by the court.

IMPORTANT POINTS TO OB-
SERVE BEFORE APPLYING AN
AGROCHEMICAL:

(a) Read the instructions and apply the
product only as prescribed. You
are compelled by law to do so,
as published in the government ga-
zette.

(b) If a recommendation is made by a
representative or agent of a com-
pany, insist that it be put in writing.

LNR-Instituut vir Graangewasse / ARC-Grain Crops Institute

(c) Save the lot number and manu-
facturing date stipulated on the
containers. Remember that no of

ficial sample may be taken from

an opened container or where the
seals have been broken, as results

will be suspect.

Your attention is drawn to the following
articles on the Act of Fertilizers, Farm
Feeds, Agricultural Remedies and Stock
Remedies no 36 of 1947 (Act 36 of
1947), www.croplife.co.za

Article 7 (1) (d)

No person shall sell any fertilize~
farm feed, agricultural remedy or stock
remedy unless it is of the composition
and efficacy specified in the application
for registration thereof possesses al
chemical, physical and other properties
so specified, and complies with the
prescribed requirements.

Article 7 (2) (a) (i)

No person shall for reward or in the
course of any industry, trade or business
use, or recommend the use of any ag-
ricultural remedy or stock remedy for a
purpose or in a manner other than that
specified on the label on a container
thereof or described on such container.

Innovation is the key to success for any seed
company and at KLEIN KAROO Seed Marketing
we are constantly developing and implementing
innovative ideas.

Our wide access to genetic diversity ensures that the
farmer will always be on the cutting edge of genetic
progress with K2 seed.

Quality is everything

that farmers receive the correct product with
high genetic purity. Seed that does not meet the
necessary requirements is destroyed.

and Europe.
